[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* In any event, I got an impression in listening to  Senator Greenwood  in this debate that he was a reluctant supporter of a Bill to outlaw <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination, and I hasten to add that I am not attempting to overstate the case. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I do not for one moment believe that  Senator Greenwood  is in favour of <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I ask the Minister for Manufacturing Industry  (Senator James McClelland)  whether it is intended to apply to the relevant authorities for the International Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of <span class="highlight">Racial</span> Discrimination to be ratified and whether that application is to be made forthwith. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* The International Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of <span class="highlight">Racial</span> Discrimination came into force as a convention in 1 969. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* The first difficulty which comes to mind is that, on a reading of the Australian Constitution, the power to make laws about <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination seems to rest with the States. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* There is certainly no express power in the Commonwealth Parliament to make laws with respect to the outlawing of <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* I refer the Minister to Article 4 which provides that adherents to the Convention are to 'condemn all propaganda and all organisations which are based on ideas or theories of superiority of one race or group of persons of one colour or ethnic origin, or which attempt to justify or promote <span class="highlight">racial</span> hatred and discrimination in any form, and undertake to adopt immediate and positive measures designed to eradicate all incitement to, or acts of, such discrimination'. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* For example, there is a requirement to declare an offence punishable by law all dissemination of ideas based on <span class="highlight">racial</span> superiority or hatred, incitement to <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination, as well as all acts of violence or incitement to such acts. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* There is also an obligation to declare illegal and to prohibit organisations and also organised and all other propaganda activities which promote and incite <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* Whatever one might say about ideas based on <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination, just as one might say a lot of things about other social or political tenets to which one can express abhorrence, in this country we have endeavoured to provide as much free speech as we can. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* They challenge freedom of speech on the justification, presumably, that such steps are necessary to abolish <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* We have seen in the United Nations how in the name of <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination countries like Rhodesia and South Africa have been treated as pariahs and have been excluded from the world community. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* Other countries which practise <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination are lauded in the United Nations and are permitted to condemn other countries while their own conduct remains unexamined. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* That means that the constitutional limitations, the general juristic limitations, on our power to deal with <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination in this country will be considered by that Committee in considering as a result of complaints whether we have complied with the terms of the Convention. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* The fact that we are attempting to deal with matters of <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination in this country does not affect the fact that people who consider themselves to be aggrieved by our laws will avail themselves of their freedom to criticise us. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* If we are to appear in the eyes of the world as a country which abhors <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination, and which does what it can to eliminate <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination, we just have to cop it sweet, to use a good old Australian expression. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* A nonracist society or a society which is trying to eliminate <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination is, I suggest, a society which can stand such criticism and which can say: 'We stand on our record and we are doing what we can to eliminate <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination. ' [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* The scheme of the Bill is that in clauses 11, 12, 13, 14, 15 and 16 there are a number of activities which are declared to be unlawful if they take place by reason of an act of <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination, as that expression is used throughout those clauses. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* What is the greater offence in the field of <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* I would put the inciter of <span class="highlight">racial</span> prejudice in an analogous position of that of the pedlar of drugs, as against the man who harbours the <span class="highlight">racial</span> poison of antisemitism or anti-colour. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* I do not see anything illogical or inconsistent in the proposition that it is more evil to incite to <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination than to practise acts of <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* Also, there is the technical matter that the Convention does require us to make incitement to <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination a criminal offence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* But, if there is the provision of services or the selling of a house and the employee or the agent commits an act of <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination in the performance of his duties, then that is the commission of an act that is unlawful. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* -Prior to the suspension of the sitting I was indicating that there can be 2 reasons why an act alleged to be an act of <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination has occurred. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* One could be because a person was in effect racially discriminating and the other could be because he regarded the provision of a service or the granting of accommodation as a credit risk which he was not prepared to undertake. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* We believe it is incumbent upon anybody who wants to take to court a person alleged to have committed a wrong to allege that the <span class="highlight">racial</span> reason, if I can put it that way, was the dominant reason and not simply to say that it was one reason. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* Perhaps the person might also take a view based on <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* It might be that the <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination is a quite substantial element but not necessarily the dominant element. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* If that is considered a wishy-washy point to make, I would refer to the sort of statistics quoted by  Senator Rae  in the second reading debate and to the statistics of the English Race Relations Commission which indicate that in that country, at least, a large number of cases are brought which are found not to be based on <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* The Commissioner has two types of fuction One is to promote an understanding and acceptance of the various programs and need for avoidance of <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* In this area of <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination, where we are making a start in this country with regard to a comprehensive law of this character, we believe it is tremendously important to tread carefully and not in an over-zealous pursuit of enforcement powers to create the possibility of a backlash that would do more harm in the long run than good. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* This makes a travesty of the efforts of an authority like this to do something about stamping out <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* It is an outright prohibition on the dissemination of ideas based on <span class="highlight">racial</span> superiority or hatred. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* I share with nobody my detestation of ideas of <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination based upon <span class="highlight">racial</span> superiority or a discrimination which seeks to evoke a superiority. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* I certainly do not believe that we should start upon the prohibition of the dissemination of ideas, even if the ideas be those of the proper promotion of <span class="highlight">racial</span> superiority, and hope that thereby we will shut out a particuar argument or a particular idea. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* I would prefer to see this clause removed entirely and I think that we do better in this area of trying to avoid <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination, of allowing the free interplay of ideas, by hoping that the tolerance which ought to be current in this community to receive and listen to differing viewpoints, no matter how antipathetic they may be to us, will be encouraged and permitted. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* The speeches of  Senator Gietzelt  and  Senator Laucke,  for example, support the proposition that no man who advances an argument which suggests there are <span class="highlight">racial</span> differences can be actuated by other than ill will. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* There are passages in those speeches which to me indicate that any proposition putting forward a <span class="highlight">racial</span> differentiation cannot be based on fact and hence must be activated by malice. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* Any doctrine of superiority based on <span class="highlight">racial</span> differentiation is scientifically false, morally condemnable, socially unjust, dangerous and without any justification. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* Their inclusion in the Bill is likely to create, as it has in Britain, an ineradicable impression in the public mind that the whole Bill is concerned with the criminal courts, fines and imprisonment; the crucial element in the whole exercise, the tackling of <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination by informal conciliation, may become de-emphasised; and public sympathy may tend to be directed more towards the discriminator, believed to be likely to receive harsh penalties, than his victim. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* In the minds of some people apparently this can cause a great feeling of <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* It is a little bit tough for such people to be called up just because they say something or publish something that somebody regards as being <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* That is an example of <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination between people of 2 coloured races. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* This <span class="highlight">racial</span> business is a very vexed question and one which is very hard to straighten out. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* Clause 29 (Inciting Acts of <span class="highlight">Racial</span> Discrimination) [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* The evils are bigotry, intolerance, <span class="highlight">racial</span> domination and suppression. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-42)

* What we have is the quiet development of a multi-<span class="highlight">racial</span> society, and it is successful. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-42)

* The same concept emerged in the recently passed <span class="highlight">Racial</span> Discrimination Bill, where the Government inserted a provision enabling legal aid and assistance to be given to persons who wanted to pursue proceedings under that legislation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750604_senate_29_s64/#debate-45)

* The Opposition amended the provision and we intended to ask this Committee to amend this provision in the same way as the Senate amended the provision for legal aid in the <span class="highlight">Racial</span> Discrimination Bill. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750604_senate_29_s64/#debate-45)

* That, as I understand the position, is the precise wording which the Senate accepted regarding legal aid provisions in the <span class="highlight">Racial</span> Discrimination Bill. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750604_senate_29_s64/#debate-45)

* Accordingly, we seek to follow the same procedure as was followed in the <span class="highlight">Racial</span> Discrimination Bill, which we think is a fair procedure. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750604_senate_29_s64/#debate-45)

* Specific reference to the Australian Legal Aid Office already exists in legislation passed by this Senate, namely, the Family Law Bill, and I cannot help thinking the objection to the specific reference to the Australian Legal Aid Office in this Bill, as with the <span class="highlight">Racial</span> Discrimination Bill which was before us a few days ago, is based on  Senator Greenwood's  recently aroused antipathy to the Australian Legal Aid Office and is not soundly based in any particular principle. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750604_senate_29_s64/#debate-45)

* It is obvious that many of the oil producing countries, many of which previously were unsophisticated in money matters, would use people from their own area, their own <span class="highlight">racial</span> groups and their own religions to develop methods of handling this money and investing it. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750612_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-30-0)

* It seems to me that it is also sensible that someone seeking funds from these areas should look to people who have had long experience in the area and who may even be of the same <span class="highlight">racial</span> group as the people in the area or even sometimes of the same religion, to seek funds, to find out where these funds come from and to investigate whether arrangements can be made to borrow some of these funds- not to borrow the money for us but to investigate the sources of the funds. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750612_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-30-0)

* We have even had an interjection of a <span class="highlight">racial</span> nature. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750612_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-30-0)

* The Country Party is advocating cuts in Aboriginal grants right around Australia because of their opposition, on <span class="highlight">racial</span> grounds, to the Aboriginal community. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750827_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-43-0)

* It will not forget the consumer protection legislation, the Trade Practices Act, which the Opposition would abolish, the <span class="highlight">Racial</span> Discrimination Bill and the Family Law Bill, which although not a Labor Government Bill was passed during the term of this Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750903_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-38-0)

* There is no unity in mind, no <span class="highlight">racial</span> unity or unity by social contact, for example, between the people of Bougainville and New Britain. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* They tend to proclaim individual freedoms, that freedom of the individual means all, but then they bay for harsh censorship laws, conscription, restricted immigration based on <span class="highlight">racial</span> grounds, and the flogging and gaoling of people like homosexuals. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750910_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-38-0)

* I ask the Minister representing the Attorney-General: Does the Government have an up-to-date estimate on when the International Convention on Elimination of all Forms of <span class="highlight">Racial</span> Discrimination is likely to enter into force for Australia? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19751007_senate_29_s66/#subdebate-28-0)

* Does the Government propose to proclaim the <span class="highlight">Racial</span> Discrimination Act as soon as possible after that Convention enters into force? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19751007_senate_29_s66/#subdebate-28-0)

* It was pointed out that the Government considers that Australian participation in events in South Africa only serves to lend respectability to the continuance of <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination in South Africa. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19751007_senate_29_s66/#subdebate-55-5)

* Thus I am informed that the South African Golf Union is an all-white organisation, and that there is also a non-<span class="highlight">racial</span> South African Golf Association which is mainly composed of coloured and Indian members, and a South African Bantu Golf Union for black people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19751007_senate_29_s66/#subdebate-55-5)

* The Australian Government is firmly opposed to <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination in any form. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19751007_senate_29_s66/#subdebate-55-5)

* The Government believes that any other approach could be taken as implicit approval or encouragement of the South African Government s policy of <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19751007_senate_29_s66/#subdebate-55-5)

* Will the <span class="highlight">Racial</span> Discrimination Act be proclaimed this month, as the article suggests, since presumably an appointment under the Act would require the Act to be proclaimed? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19751009_senate_29_s66/#subdebate-23-0)

* As the honourable senator will be aware, sections 1, 2 and 7 of the <span class="highlight">Racial</span> Discrimination Act have already come into operation but the rest of the Act has not yet come into force. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19751009_senate_29_s66/#subdebate-23-0)

* It is related to another matter which is part of the honourable senator's question, that is, the date of coming into force in Australia of the International Convention on the Elimination of all Forms of <span class="highlight">Racial</span> Discrimination. * <span class="highlight">Racial</span> Discrimination Bill 1975 [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19751015_senate_29_s66/#subdebate-37-0)

* We the members of the National Congress of the Aboriginal people and the Torres Strait Islanders, assembled at Canberra, Australia this 10th day of March 1 976, do hereby, as the democratically elected representatives of our people, solemnly and unanimously resolve that we claim for our people the following inalienable rights:- the right to natural justice, the right to self determination as a separate and distinct people, with our own laws and customs, languages culture and heritage, living in our ancient home-land and with the right to a full voice in and influence on our own affairs, the right to be free from the <span class="highlight">racial</span> oppression and discrimination imposed upon us by the uninvited European people who have invaded our country and imposed their own laws and way of life upon us, the right to preserve in perpetuity for our people the surviving tribal lands reserves and sacred sites in all Australian states and territories, the right to fair and just compensation to our scattered tribes, our detribalised and urban people, for the lands seized from our forefathers, and for the inhuman and violent treatment of our people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760325_senate_30_s67/#subdebate-57-0)

* In addition to this Act, the <span class="highlight">Racial</span> Discrimination Act became effective in law from 31 October 1975. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760817_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-37-18)

* This Act has a more general application to discrimination based on race, colour, descent or national or ethnic origin, and makes it unlawful for a person to do an act involving <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination which impairs the enjoyment, on an equal footing of fundamental rights and freedoms. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760817_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-37-18)

* This Act also prescribes acts of <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination in respect of access to places and facilities available to members of the public, the disposal of land, housing and other accommodation, the provision of goods and services to the public, employment, and the right to join trade unions. * The Human Rights Commission Bill and the <span class="highlight">Racial</span> Discrimination Amendment Bill, which are connected pieces of legislation, have been in gestation for quite a long time. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* I think that we can make alterations to the Human Rights Commission Bill which will turn the proposed Commission into an organisation which can be effective, but I do not see any way in which we can deal with the other Bill, the <span class="highlight">Racial</span> Discrimination Amendment Bill, which has been criticised so vehemently by  Senator Evans  this afternoon. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* Last year the Australian Government submitted to the World Conference to Combat Racism and <span class="highlight">Racial</span> Discrimination a national report which stated that action taken in this country to combat <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination had been based on five principles. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* <span class="highlight">Racial</span> discrimination should be made unlawful by specific legislation; [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* Formal administrative machinery should be established for the investigation of <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination on a systematic basis and to attempt to settle issues involving discrimination by conciliation; [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* A comprehensive framework of legally enforceable remedies should be created to provide redress against <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination where conciliation fails. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* I do not believe that we have adequately enforced that <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination covenant as yet. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* The Commissioner for Community Relations, who already has specific responsibilities in the area of <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination, is not named as a Human Rights Commissioner and it is clear to me that he will not be appointed to such a position. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* There is indeed a case for amalgamating the operations concerning <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination with other human rights (as the Galbally Report recommends), but not by downgrading the existing working operations of the <span class="highlight">Racial</span> Discrimination Act and debarring its Commissioner from the policy determinations of the Commission. * In most of these cases, particularly where <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination or breaches of human rights occur, it is the most unfortunate people, economically, educationally and in other ways, who would not have the wherewithal to be able to carry out that kind of prosecution. * I have said time and time again that in relation to stamping out discrimination the <span class="highlight">Racial</span> Discrimination Act of 1975 has always seemed to me to be a toothless tiger as I have always felt that in most instances discrimination is a state of mind, an inherent belief, which can be eliminated only by reason, greater knowledge, tolerance and understanding. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* I am confining most of my remarks to the <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination aspects of these two Bills. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* I say that because I disagree with the amendments to the <span class="highlight">Racial</span> Discrimination Act which will bring the Commissioner for Community Relations under the new Commission. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* He will have no way of doing things on his own behalf, as he has been doing by travelling around the country and setting up in different towns voluntary organisations of groups of people who are interested in looking into acts of <span class="highlight">racial</span> discrimination. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)
